                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer395212628" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer57649341627109944">
                    Normally, I don't write reviews but felt compelled to now as I absolutely loved this book. I am surprised to read its contents, which are almost news for me. It's erudite, witty, imaginative and packed with great ideas. I'm a person who has often been drawn to aspects of religion, but couldn't really articulate why. In clear, illuminating prose, this wonderful book has explained why ancient people crafted religions. It also gave me loads of food for thought. Apart from exposing the illusion of g
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText57649341627109944" style="display:none">
                    Normally, I don't write reviews but felt compelled to now as I absolutely loved this book. I am surprised to read its contents, which are almost news for me. It's erudite, witty, imaginative and packed with great ideas. I'm a person who has often been drawn to aspects of religion, but couldn't really articulate why. In clear, illuminating prose, this wonderful book has explained why ancient people crafted religions. It also gave me loads of food for thought. Apart from exposing the illusion of gods, it explains the impact of the concept of gods on humans today. This book has shattered my faith. It is a painful experience to know that whatever I knew about gods was illusion; I am no longer protected by a savior God. In the long run this may help me to believe myself.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="57649341627109944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>
                 </div>

                   <span id="freeTextContainer3205055050643046116">
                    This book unfortunately did not live up to its potential. The author has made a series of statements which, though sensible on the surface, are unsupported by evidence, and used combinations of those statements to make assertions which are in many cases quite a leap of logic. Some chapters were more interesting - for example those on the adaptation of various religions to changing times - but overall this is not a book I'd recommend.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    *Goodreads First Read Review*

               <div class="review" id="review_999687366" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/999687366" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33160189-sumathy" title="Sumathy">
                 <img alt="Sumathy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/999687366?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Sep 11, 2014
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/33160189-sumathy" title="Sumathy">
                   Sumathy
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">
                   4 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                  <span class="greyText">
                   
                  </span>
                  <a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/20490631-the-evolution-of-gods" title="Kindle Edition ">
                   review of another edition
                  </a>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33160189-sumathy?shelf=for-blog">
                    for-blog
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer999687366" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer6398057668669329025">
                    Methodically illustrates the evolution of Gods. In the process, busts lot of myths. Enlightening read and makes one accept that we may continue to follow certain practices but that is our own creation and not handed down by somebody from heaven!
                   </span>
                  </span>
                 </div>

               <script charset="utf-8" type="text/javascript">
                function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TwDNr9bSGwbUtjlOcY7ZGG0TDo6sL+k0+YBhTl2EQFb7Xczbznj+15y/ztPQFvCQhtqk/7UBsvUcrevgCiZLuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GrkssH08pTrNpY2dHpxpgMVMbMRuUSsztzxrDcmNEquu5C3EZZZA64WsegC/BEAILoXGtXd/cPJSEeGjni8ZRA==')})
  }

He is faced with the challenge of finding a lasting solution to the Kashmir crisis. \nWhich Biblical Weapon was Tested in Shaksgam Valley? Why is Mansur Haider Important? Dozakhnama: Conversations in Hell is an extraordinary novel, a biography of Manto and Ghalib and a history of Indian culture rolled into one. Exhumed from dust, Mantos unpublished novel surfaces in Lucknow. Is it real or is it a fake? In this dastan, Manto and Ghalib converse, entwining their lives in shared dreams. The result is an intellectual journey that takes us into the people and events that shape us as a culture. As one writer describes it, I discovered Rabisankar Bal like a torch in the darkness of the history of this subcontinent. This is the real story of two centuries of our own country. Rabisankar Bals audacious novel, told by reflections in a mirror and forged in the fires of hell, is both an oral tale and a shield against oblivion. An echo of distant screams.                 <img alt="Bombay Stories" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/books/1354099123m/16176948.jpg"/>

               <script>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_16176948'), "\n\n  &lt;h2&gt;&lt;a class=\"readable\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16176948-bombay-stories?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\"&gt;Bombay Stories&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;\/h2&gt;\n\n      &lt;div&gt;\n        by &lt;a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/263878.Saadat_Hasan_Manto?a=7&amp;origin=related_works\"&gt;Saadat Hasan Manto&lt;\/a&gt;\n      &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n          &lt;div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\"&gt;\n            &lt;span class=\"minirating\"&gt;&lt;span class=\"stars staticStars\"&gt;&lt;a class=\"staticStar p10\" size=\"12x12\" title=\"3.72 of 5 stars\"&gt;3.72 of 5 stars&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;a class=\"staticStar p10\" size=\"12x12\" title=\"3.72 of 5 stars\"&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;a class=\"staticStar p10\" size=\"12x12\" title=\"3.72 of 5 stars\"&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;a class=\"staticStar p6\" size=\"12x12\" title=\"3.72 of 5 stars\"&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;a class=\"staticStar p0\" size=\"12x12\" title=\"3.72 of 5 stars\"&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;\/span&gt; 3.72 avg rating &mdash; 267 ratings&lt;\/span&gt;            &mdash; published 2014\n          &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n    &lt;div class=\"addBookTipDescription\"&gt;\n      \n&lt;span id=\"freeTextContainer7719561632902821215\"&gt;Bombay in the 1930s and 1940s reigned as the undisputed cosmopolitan capital of the Subcontinent. Bombay Stories is a collection of Mantos work from his years in the city. Freshly arrived in 1930s Mumbai, Manto saw a city like no otheran exhilarati&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText7719561632902821215\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Bombay in the 1930s and 1940s reigned as the undisputed cosmopolitan capital of the Subcontinent. Bombay Stories is a collection of Mantos work from his years in the city. Freshly arrived in 1930s Mumbai, Manto saw a city like no otheran exhilarating hub of license and liberty, and a city bursting with both creative energy and helpless despondency. It was to be Mantos favourite city, and he was among the first to write the Bombay characters we are now familiar with from countless stories and filmsprostitutes, pimps, lowlifes, writers, intellectuals, aspiring film actors, thugs, conmen and crooks. His hard-edged, moving stories remain, a hundred years after his birth, startling and provocative?in searching out those forgotten by humanity, Manto wrote about what it means to be human. Matt Reeck and Aftab Ahmads translations reach into the streets and capture in contemporary, idiomatic English the feeling that Urdus most celebrated short-story writers work stories provide in the Through this book I offer my readers a glimpse into the multifaceted world of schizophrenia in the form of fictitious storyline revolving around two characters Monty (the psychotic part)  and Virginia (the non psychotic part). The boundary between the two is permeable. Monty conjures up Gulabi, following his abrupt separation from his long time partner, while Virginia, having suffered from a personal loss sets out to follow her lifelong aspiration to travel the           <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
           <span class="readable">
            All the three monotheist religions (Jewish, Christianity and Islam)claim that their God (Yahweh, God and Allah) created humans in a similar way: this indicates that creationist have not yet established the creator.
           </span>
           <nobr>
            
            <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1197647-all-the-three-monotheist-religions-jewish-christianity-and-islam-claim-that">
             1 likes
            </a>
           </nobr>
           <div class="clear">
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
           <span class="readable">
            However, regarding sacrifices, one irony persists almost universally: the act of sacrifice was just opposite to its motive. People killed someone to appease so-called kind and merciful gods. How could a major intelligentsia of the earth conceive that the killing of an innocent being could appease a god, who was supposed to be kind?
           </span>
           <nobr>
            
            <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1283879-however-regarding-sacrifices-one-irony-persists-almost-universally-the-act">
             0 likes
            </a>
           </nobr>
